href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a></span> 9\xe2\x80\x930 <a class="mw-selflink selflink">Wales</a><span class="flagicon">&#160;<img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Flag_of_Wales_%281807%E2%80%931953%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_Wales_%281807%E2%80%931953%29.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Flag_of_Wales_%281807%E2%80%931953%29.svg/46px-Flag_of_Wales_%281807%E2%80%931953%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="996" data-file-height="498" /></span><br />(<a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, Scotland; 23 March 1878)</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">World Cup</a></th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Appearances</th><td>\n1 (<i>first in <a href="/wiki/1958_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1958 FIFA World Cup">1958</a></i>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Best result</th><td>\nQuarter-finals, <a href="/wiki/1958_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1958 FIFA World Cup">1958</a></td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship" title="UEFA European Championship">European Championship</a></th></tr><tr><th scope="row">Appearances</th><td>\n1 (<i>first in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">2016</a></i>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Best result</th><td>\nSemi-finals, <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">2016</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Wales national football team</b> (<a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>: <i lang="cy">T\xc3\xaem p\xc3\xaal-droed cenedlaethol Cymru</i>) represents <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a> in international <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>. It is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Football_Association_of_Wales" title="Football Association of Wales">Football Association of Wales</a> (FAW), the governing body for <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Wales" title="Football in Wales">football in Wales</a> and the third-oldest national football association in the world.\n</p><p>Although part of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, Wales has always had a representative side that plays in major professional tournaments, though not in the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>, as the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> has always recognised United Kingdom representative sides.\n</p><p>During their history, Wales have qualified for two major international tournaments. They reached the quarter-finals of the <a href="/wiki/1958_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1958 FIFA World Cup">1958 FIFA World Cup</a> and reached the semi-finals of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">UEFA Euro 2016</a>. Wales also progressed through <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1976_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 1976 qualifying">UEFA Euro 1976 qualifying</a> to the quarter-final, which was played on a home and away leg basis, but they did not feature in the finals tournament.\n</p><p>At all levels, including the youth teams, the Welsh national team draws players primarily from clubs in the <a href="/wiki/English_football_league_system" title="English football league system">English football league system</a>. The main professional Welsh clubs play in the English leagues, with some full-time and part-time professional clubs playing in the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_football_league_system" title="Welsh football league system">Welsh football league system</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_early_years">The early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: The early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wales_V_Scotland_3386999.tif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Wales_V_Scotland_3386999.tif/lossy-page1-150px-Wales_V_Scotland_3386999.tif.jpg" width="150" height="315" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Wales_V_Scotland_3386999.tif/lossy-page1-225px-Wales_V_Scotland_3386999.tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Wales_V_Scotland_3386999.tif/lossy-page1-300px-Wales_V_Scotland_3386999.tif.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1151" data-file-height="2414" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wales_V_Scotland_3386999.tif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Report of <i>The Cardiff Times</i> about Wales\' first competitive match against Scotland in 1876.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wales_national_team_1887.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Wales_national_team_1887.jpg/250px-Wales_national_team_1887.jpg" width="250" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Wales_national_team_1887.jpg/375px-Wales_national_team_1887.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Wales_national_team_1887.jpg/500px-Wales_national_team_1887.jpg 2x" data-file-width="976" data-file-height="549" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wales_national_team_1887.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Wales side of 1887\xe2\x80\x9388.</div></div></div>\n<p>Wales played its <a href="/wiki/Scotland_v_Wales_(1876)" class="mw-redirect" title="Scotland v Wales (1876)">first competitive match</a> on 25 March 1876 against <a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_football_team" title="Scotland national football team">Scotland</a> in <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, making it the third oldest international football team in the world. Although the Scots won the first fixture 4\xe2\x80\x930, a return match was planned in Wales the following year, and so it was that the first international football match on Welsh soil took place at The Racecourse Ground, <a href="/wiki/Wrexham" title="Wrexham">Wrexham</a>, on 5 March 1877. Scotland took the spoils winning 2\xe2\x80\x930. Wales\' first match against <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> came in 1879, a 2\xe2\x80\x931 defeat at the <a href="/wiki/Kennington_Oval" class="mw-redirect" title="Kennington Oval">Kennington Oval</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, and in 1882, Wales faced <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Northern Ireland national football team">Ireland</a> for the first time, winning 7\xe2\x80\x931 in Wrexham.\n</p><p>The associations of the four <a href="/wiki/Home_Nations" title="Home Nations">Home Nations</a> met in <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a> on 6 December 1882 to set down a set of worldwide rules. This meeting saw the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/International_Football_Association_Board" title="International Football Association Board">International Football Association Board</a> (IFAB) to approve changes to the rules, a task the four associations still perform to this day. The 1883\xe2\x80\x9384 season saw the formation of the <a href="/wiki/British_Home_Championship" title="British Home Championship">British Home Championship</a>, a tournament which was played annually between England, Scotland, Ireland and Wales, until 1983\xe2\x80\x9384.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Wales were champions on 12 occasions, winning outright seven times whilst sharing the title five times.\n</p><p>The FAW became members of <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>, world football\'s governing body, in 1906, but the relationship between FIFA and the British associations was fraught and the British nations withdrew from FIFA in 1928 in a dispute over payments to <a href="/wiki/Amateur" title="Amateur">amateur</a> players. As a result, Wales did not enter the first three <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cups</a>. In 1932, Wales played host to the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland_national_football_team" title="Republic of Ireland national football team">Republic of Ireland</a>, the first time they played against a side from outside the four home nations. One year later, Wales played a match outside the United Kingdom for the first time when they travelled to <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a> to play <a href="/wiki/France_national_football_team" title="France national football team">France national football team</a> in a match drawn 1\xe2\x80\x931. After <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Wales, along with the other three home nations, rejoined FIFA in 1946 and took part in the qualifying rounds for the <a href="/wiki/1950_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1950 FIFA World Cup">1950 World Cup</a>, the 1949\xe2\x80\x9350 Home Championships being designated as a qualifying group. The top two teams were to qualify for the finals in Brazil, but Wales finished bottom of the group.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1958_World_Cup">1958 World Cup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1958 World Cup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Charles,_Wales_versus_Scotland,_Ninian_Park,_1954.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/John_Charles%2C_Wales_versus_Scotland%2C_Ninian_Park%2C_1954.jpg/170px-John_Charles%2C_Wales_versus_Scotland%2C_Ninian_Park%2C_1954.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/John_Charles%2C_Wales_versus_Scotland%2C_Ninian_Park%2C_1954.jpg/255px-John_Charles%2C_Wales_versus_Scotland%2C_Ninian_Park%2C_1954.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/John_Charles%2C_Wales_versus_Scotland%2C_Ninian_Park%2C_1954.jpg/340px-John_Charles%2C_Wales_versus_Scotland%2C_Ninian_Park%2C_1954.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2778" data-file-height="3707" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Charles,_Wales_versus_Scotland,_Ninian_Park,_1954.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/John_Charles" title="John Charles">John Charles</a> on international duty for Wales, against Scotland, 1954</div></div></div>\n<p>The 1950s were a golden age for Welsh football with stars such as <a href="/wiki/Ivor_Allchurch" title="Ivor Allchurch">Ivor Allchurch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Jones_(Welsh_footballer)" title="Cliff Jones (Welsh footballer)">Cliff Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alf_Sherwood" title="Alf Sherwood">Alf Sherwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Kelsey" title="Jack Kelsey">Jack Kelsey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Ford" title="Trevor Ford">Trevor Ford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ron_Burgess_(footballer)" title="Ron Burgess (footballer)">Ronnie Burgess</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terry_Medwin" title="Terry Medwin">Terry Medwin</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Charles" title="John Charles">John Charles</a>.\n</p><p>Wales made its only World Cup finals tournament appearance in the <a href="/wiki/1958_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1958 FIFA World Cup">1958 edition</a> in Sweden. However, their path to qualification was unusual. Having finished second to <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia_national_football_team" title="Czechoslovakia national football team">Czechoslovakia</a> in qualifying Group 4, the golden generation of Welsh football managed by <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Murphy_(footballer)" title="Jimmy Murphy (footballer)">Jimmy Murphy</a> seemed to have missed out on qualification, but the politics of the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> subsequently intervened. In the Asian/African qualifying zone, <a href="/wiki/Egypt_national_football_team" title="Egypt national football team">Egypt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sudan_national_football_team" title="Sudan national football team">Sudan</a> had refused to play against <a href="/wiki/Israel_national_football_team" title="Israel national football team">Israel</a> following the <a href="/wiki/Suez_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Suez crisis">Suez crisis</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Indonesia_national_football_team" title="Indonesia national football team">Indonesia</a> had insisted on meeting Israel on neutral ground. As a result, FIFA proclaimed Israel winners of their respective group. However, FIFA did not want a team to qualify for the World Cup finals without actually playing a match, and so lots were drawn of all the second-placed teams in <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a>. <a href="/wiki/Belgium_national_football_team" title="Belgium national football team">Belgium</a> were drawn out first but refused to participate, and so then Wales was drawn out and awarded a two-legged play-off match against Israel with a place in Sweden for the winners.<sup id="cite_ref-history_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Having defeated Israel 2\xe2\x80\x930 at the <a href="/wiki/Ramat_Gan_Stadium" title="Ramat Gan Stadium">Ramat Gan Stadium</a> and 2\xe2\x80\x930 at <a href="/wiki/Ninian_Park" title="Ninian Park">Ninian Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>, Wales went through to a World Cup finals tournament for the first\xe2\x80\x94and currently only\xe2\x80\x94time.\n</p><p>The strong <a href="/wiki/1958_FIFA_World_Cup_squads" title="1958 FIFA World Cup squads">Welsh squad</a> made their mark in Sweden, drawing all the matches in their group against <a href="/wiki/Hungary_national_football_team" title="Hungary national football team">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweden_national_football_team" title="Sweden national football team">Sweden</a> before defeating Hungary in a play-off match to reach the quarter-finals against <a href="/wiki/Brazilian_national_football_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Brazilian national football team">Brazil</a>. However, Wales\' chances of victory against Brazil were hampered by an injury to John Charles that ruled him out of the match. Wales lost 1\xe2\x80\x930 with 17-year-old <a href="/wiki/Pel%C3%A9" title="Pel\xc3\xa9">Pel\xc3\xa9</a> scoring his first international goal. The goal made Pel\xc3\xa9 the youngest World Cup goalscorer and Brazil went on to win the tournament.\n</p><p>Wales\' remarkable campaign in Sweden was the subject of the best-selling book <i>When Pele Broke Our Hearts: Wales and the 1958 World Cup</i> (by Mario Risoli, St David\'s Press) which was published on the 40th anniversary of the World Cup and was also the inspiration for a Bafta Cymru-nominated documentary.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1970s">1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Wales had never qualified for the finals tournament of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championship" title="UEFA European Championship">UEFA European Championship</a> since its inception in 1960. However, in 1976, the team managed by <a href="/wiki/Mike_Smith_(football_manager)" title="Mike Smith (football manager)">Mike Smith</a> reached the last eight of the competition, having finished top of qualifying Group 2 ahead of Hungary, <a href="/wiki/Austria_national_football_team" title="Austria national football team">Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_national_football_team" title="Luxembourg national football team">Luxembourg</a>. \n</p><p>Prior to 1980, only four countries qualified for the finals tournament, and Wales were drawn to play against the winners of Group 3\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia_national_football_team" title="Yugoslavia national football team">Yugoslavia</a>\xe2\x80\x94on a home and away basis match. Wales lost the first leg 2\xe2\x80\x930 in <a href="/wiki/Zagreb" title="Zagreb">Zagreb</a> and were eliminated from the competition following a 1\xe2\x80\x931 draw in a bad-tempered return leg at Ninian Park, Cardiff, which was marred by crowd trouble. This initially led to Wales\' ban from the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1980" title="UEFA Euro 1980">1980</a> tournament. However, the ban was reduced on appeal to a four-year ban on qualifying matches being played within 100 miles of Cardiff. Yugoslavia went on to finish third in the 1980 tournament.\n</p><p>The following year, Wales defeated England on English soil for the first time in 42 years and secured their only victory to date at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a> thanks to a <a href="/wiki/Leighton_James" title="Leighton James">Leighton James</a> penalty. Another notable achievement came in the <a href="/wiki/1980_British_Home_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="1980 British Home Championship">1980 British Home Championship</a>, as Wales comprehensively defeated England at The Racecourse Ground, Wrexham. Goals from <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Thomas_(football)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mickey Thomas (football)">Mickey Thomas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Walsh_(footballer)" title="Ian Walsh (footballer)">Ian Walsh</a>, Leighton James and an own goal by <a href="/wiki/Phil_Thompson" title="Phil Thompson">Phil Thompson</a> saw Wales defeat England 4\xe2\x80\x931 just four days after England had defeated the then-world champions, <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s">1980s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1980s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="1982 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">1982 FIFA World Cup qualifiers</a> the Wales team managed by <a href="/wiki/Mike_England" title="Mike England">Mike England</a> came extremely close to qualification: a 3\xe2\x80\x930 defeat against the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union_national_football_team" title="Soviet Union national football team">Soviet Union</a> in their final match meant they missed out on goal difference, but the real damage had been done by their failure to beat <a href="/wiki/Iceland_national_football_team" title="Iceland national football team">Iceland</a> in their last home match, the match eventually finishing 2\xe2\x80\x932 after several hold-ups due to floodlight failures.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Mark_Hughes" title="Mark Hughes">Mark Hughes</a> marked his debut for Wales by scoring the only goal of the match as England were defeated once again in 1984. The following season, Hughes was again on target, scoring a wonder goal as Wales thrashed <a href="/wiki/Spain_national_football_team" title="Spain national football team">Spain</a> 3\xe2\x80\x930 at The Racecourse during qualification for the <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986 World Cup</a>. However, despite defeating Scotland 1\xe2\x80\x930 at Hampden Park, it was again Iceland that wrecked Welsh hopes by defeating Wales 1\xe2\x80\x930 in <a href="/wiki/Reykjav%C3%ADk" title="Reykjav\xc3\xadk">Reykjav\xc3\xadk</a>, and for the second World Cup in a row, Wales missed out on goal difference. Wales had to win their last match at home to Scotland to be guaranteed at least a play-off, but were held to a 1\xe2\x80\x931 draw in a <a href="/wiki/1985_Wales_v_Scotland_football_match" title="1985 Wales v Scotland football match">match</a> marred by the death of Scotland manager <a href="/wiki/Jock_Stein" title="Jock Stein">Jock Stein</a>, who collapsed from a heart attack at the end of the match.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1990s">1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Under <a href="/wiki/Terry_Yorath" title="Terry Yorath">Terry Yorath</a>, Wales attained what was then their highest <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">FIFA world ranking</a> on 27 August 1993. Again Wales came close to qualifying for a major championship when they came within a whisker of reaching the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994 World Cup</a>. Needing to win the final match of the group at home to <a href="/wiki/Romania_national_football_team" title="Romania national football team">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Bodin" title="Paul Bodin">Paul Bodin</a> missed a penalty when the scores were level 1\xe2\x80\x931; the miss was immediately followed by Romania taking the lead and going on to win 2\xe2\x80\x931.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the failure to qualify, Yorath\'s contract as manager of the national side was not renewed by the FAW, and <a href="/wiki/John_Toshack" title="John Toshack">John Toshack</a>\xe2\x80\x94the then-manager of <a href="/wiki/Real_Sociedad" title="Real Sociedad">Real Sociedad</a>\xe2\x80\x94was appointed on a part-time basis. However, Toshack resigned after just one match\xe2\x80\x94a 3\xe2\x80\x931 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Norway_national_football_team" title="Norway national football team">Norway</a>\xe2\x80\x94citing problems with the FAW as his reason for leaving, although he was sure to have been shocked at being booed off the pitch at Ninian Park by the Welsh fans still reeling from the dismissal of Yorath.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Mike Smith took the manager role for the second time at the start of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_1996" title="UEFA Euro 1996">Euro 1996</a> qualifiers, but Wales slipped to embarrassing defeats against <a href="/wiki/Moldova_national_football_team" title="Moldova national football team">Moldova</a> and <a href="/wiki/Georgia_national_football_team" title="Georgia national football team">Georgia</a> before <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Gould" title="Bobby Gould">Bobby Gould</a> was appointed in June 1995.\n</p><p>Gould\'s time in charge of Wales is seen as a dark period by Welsh football fans. His questionable tactics and public fallings-out with players <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Blake" title="Nathan Blake">Nathan Blake</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Savage" title="Robbie Savage">Robbie Savage</a><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and Mark Hughes<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>, coupled with embarrassing defeats to club side <a href="/wiki/Leyton_Orient_F.C." title="Leyton Orient F.C.">Leyton Orient</a> and a 7\xe2\x80\x931 thrashing by the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Netherlands</a> in 1996 did not make him a popular figure within Wales. Gould finally resigned following a 4\xe2\x80\x930 defeat to <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> in 1999, and the FAW turned to two legends of the national team, <a href="/wiki/Neville_Southall" title="Neville Southall">Neville Southall</a> and Mark Hughes, to take temporary charge of the match against <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a> four days later, with Hughes later being appointed on a permanent basis.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2000s">2000s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2000s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Under Mark Hughes, Wales came close to qualifying for a place at <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004" title="UEFA Euro 2004">Euro 2004</a> in Portugal, being narrowly defeated by <a href="/wiki/Russia_national_football_team" title="Russia national football team">Russia</a> in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2004_qualifying_play-offs" title="UEFA Euro 2004 qualifying play-offs">the play-offs</a>. However, the defeat was not without its controversy, as Russian midfielder <a href="/wiki/Yegor_Titov" title="Yegor Titov">Yegor Titov</a> tested positive for the use of a banned substance after the first qualifying leg,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> a scoreless draw in <a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>. Notwithstanding, FIFA opted not to take action against the <a href="/wiki/Football_Union_of_Russia" class="mw-redirect" title="Football Union of Russia">Football Union of Russia</a> other than instructing them not to field Titov again, and the Russian team went on to defeat Wales 1\xe2\x80\x930 in Cardiff to qualify for the final tournament.\n</p><p>Following a disappointing start to <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_6" title="2006 FIFA World Cup qualification \xe2\x80\x93 UEFA Group 6">2006 FIFA World Cup qualification \xe2\x80\x93 UEFA Group 6</a>, Hughes left his role with the national team to take over as manager of English <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> outfit <a href="/wiki/Blackburn_Rovers_F.C." title="Blackburn Rovers F.C.">Blackburn Rovers</a>. On 12 November 2004, John Toshack was appointed manager for the second time.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2008 qualifying">Euro 2008 qualifying</a>, Wales were drawn in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008_qualifying_Group_D" title="UEFA Euro 2008 qualifying Group D">Group D</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic_national_football_team" title="Czech Republic national football team">Czech Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Slovakia_national_football_team" title="Slovakia national football team">Slovakia</a>, the Republic of Ireland, <a href="/wiki/Cyprus_national_football_team" title="Cyprus national football team">Cyprus</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Marino_national_football_team" title="San Marino national football team">San Marino</a>. The team\'s performance was disappointing, finishing fifth in the group with expected defeat at home to Germany yet an unexpected draw away, a loss away and a goalless draw at home to the Czech Republic, a loss away and 2\xe2\x80\x932 draw at home to the Republic of Ireland, a 3\xe2\x80\x930 home win and uninspiring 2\xe2\x80\x931 away win against minnows San Marino, a 3\xe2\x80\x931 home win and 3\xe2\x80\x931 away defeat against Cyprus, and a spectacularly mixed performance against Slovakia, losing 5\xe2\x80\x931 at home and winning 5\xe2\x80\x932 away. However, better performances towards the end of the competition by a team containing\xe2\x80\x94of necessity because of injuries and suspensions of senior players\xe2\x80\x94no fewer than five players who were eligible for selection for the under-21 squad was viewed as a hopeful sign of future progress for the team.\n</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_4" title="2010 FIFA World Cup qualification \xe2\x80\x93 UEFA Group 4">2010 FIFA World Cup qualification \xe2\x80\x93 UEFA Group 4</a>, Wales made a promising start, winning 1\xe2\x80\x930 and 2\xe2\x80\x930 against <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan_national_football_team" title="Azerbaijan national football team">Azerbaijan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein_national_football_team" title="Liechtenstein national football team">Liechtenstein</a>, respectively. However, they lost their next match against Russia in Moscow, 2\xe2\x80\x931, after <a href="/wiki/Joe_Ledley" title="Joe Ledley">Joe Ledley</a> had briefly drawn them level. The qualifying campaign showed signs of promise when the team managed to prevent Germany from scoring for 74 minutes of their match in <a href="/wiki/M%C3%B6nchengladbach" title="M\xc3\xb6nchengladbach">M\xc3\xb6nchengladbach</a>, although Wales ultimately lost 1\xe2\x80\x930. Two 2\xe2\x80\x930 home defeats by <a href="/wiki/Finland_national_football_team" title="Finland national football team">Finland</a> and Germany in Spring 2009 effectively put paid to Wales\' hopes of qualification.\n</p><p>Wales were drawn in <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012_qualifying_Group_G" title="UEFA Euro 2012 qualifying Group G">UEFA Euro 2012 qualifying Group G</a> with <a href="/wiki/Montenegro_national_football_team" title="Montenegro national football team">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_national_football_team" title="Bulgaria national football team">Bulgaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Switzerland_national_football_team" title="Switzerland national football team">Switzerland</a> and close rivals England. Wales lost 1\xe2\x80\x930 away to Montenegro in their opening match and, on 9 September 2010, John Toshack stood down as manager after being disappointed at previous results in 2010 against <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_football_team" title="Croatia national football team">Croatia</a> and the opening Euro 2012 qualifier.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Wales_national_under-21_football_team" title="Wales national under-21 football team">Wales under-21</a> coach <a href="/wiki/Brian_Flynn" title="Brian Flynn">Brian Flynn</a> took over from Toshack as caretaker manager with a view to a possible permanent appointment, but a 1\xe2\x80\x930 home defeat to Bulgaria and 4\xe2\x80\x931 away loss to Switzerland prompted the FAW to pass over Flynn.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2010s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wales_national_football_team.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Wales_national_football_team.jpg/220px-Wales_national_football_team.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Wales_national_football_team.jpg/330px-Wales_national_football_team.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Wales_national_football_team.jpg/440px-Wales_national_football_team.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2352" data-file-height="1568" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wales_national_football_team.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Wales team on 11 October 2011 ahead of their <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2012 qualifying">UEFA Euro 2012 qualifying</a> match against <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria_national_football_team" title="Bulgaria national football team">Bulgaria</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sofia" title="Sofia">Sofia</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Gary_Speed" title="Gary Speed">Gary Speed</a> was appointed as permanent manager on 14 December 2010. Speed\'s first match as manager was 8 February 2011 in the inaugural <a href="/wiki/2011_Nations_Cup" title="2011 Nations Cup">Nations Cup</a>, which the Republic of Ireland won 3\xe2\x80\x930.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Speed\'s first competitive match was the Euro 2012 qualifier at home to England on 26 March 2011, and Speed appointed 20-year-old <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Ramsey" title="Aaron Ramsey">Aaron Ramsey</a> captain, making him the youngest Wales captain. Wales lost to England 2\xe2\x80\x930 and in August 2011 Wales attained their lowest FIFA ranking of 117th. This was followed by a 2\xe2\x80\x931 home win against Montenegro, a 1\xe2\x80\x930 away loss to England, a 2\xe2\x80\x930 home win against Switzerland and a 1\xe2\x80\x930 away win against Bulgaria. Consequently, in October 2011, Wales had rapidly risen to 45th in the FIFA rankings. A 4\xe2\x80\x931 home win in a friendly match against Norway on 12 November 2011 proved to be Speed\'s last match in charge of Wales. The match was a culmination of Speed\'s efforts which led Wales to receive the unofficial award for biggest mover of 2011 in the FIFA rankings.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> His tenure as manager ended in tragic circumstances two weeks later when he was found dead at his home on 27 November, having apparently committed suicide.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Due to <a href="/wiki/London_bid_for_the_2012_Summer_Olympic_and_Paralympic_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="London bid for the 2012 Summer Olympic and Paralympic Games">London\'s successful bid</a> for the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a>, a Great Britain team would qualify as of right of being the host nation. However, the FAW stressed it was strongly against the proposal.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Despite this, Welsh players Aaron Ramsey and <a href="/wiki/Gareth_Bale" title="Gareth Bale">Gareth Bale</a> expressed their interest in representing the <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_Olympic_football_team" title="Great Britain Olympic football team">Great Britain Olympic football team</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Bale was ultimately omitted due to injury,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> but Ramsey was joined by four other Welshmen in <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Pearce" title="Stuart Pearce">Stuart Pearce</a>\'s 18-man squad: <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Joe_Allen" title="Joe Allen">Joe Allen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neil_Taylor_(footballer)" title="Neil Taylor (footballer)">Neil Taylor</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Giggs" title="Ryan Giggs">Ryan Giggs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Craig_Bellamy" title="Craig Bellamy">Craig Bellamy</a> were included as over-age players, with Giggs being made captain.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Chris_Coleman_(footballer)" title="Chris Coleman (footballer)">Chris Coleman</a> was appointed Wales team manager on 19 January 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> For <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_(UEFA)" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)">2014 World Cup qualification</a>, Wales were drawn in <a href="/wiki/2014_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_A" title="2014 FIFA World Cup qualification \xe2\x80\x93 UEFA Group A">Group A</a> with Croatia, <a href="/wiki/Serbia_national_football_team" title="Serbia national football team">Serbia</a>, Belgium, Scotland and Macedonia. They lost their first match 2\xe2\x80\x930, against Belgium. Their second match, against Serbia, was even worse, finishing 6\xe2\x80\x931, Wales\'s worst defeat since the 7\xe2\x80\x931 reversal to the Netherlands in 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In October 2012, <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Williams_(footballer)" title="Ashley Williams (footballer)">Ashley Williams</a> was appointed captain of Wales by Coleman, replacing Aaron Ramsey.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Wales won at home against Scotland 2\xe2\x80\x931, lost away to Croatia 2\xe2\x80\x930 and won away against Scotland 2\xe2\x80\x931, but a 2\xe2\x80\x931 loss at home to Croatia ended Wales hopes of qualifying.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Wales were placed in Group B for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying">qualifying</a> for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">Euro 2016</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Andorra_national_football_team" title="Andorra national football team">Andorra</a>, Belgium, <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina_national_football_team" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina national football team">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, Cyprus and Israel. In July 2015, following four wins and two draws, Wales topped the group.\n</p><p>In July 2015, having attained their then highest FIFA ranking of tenth,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Wales were placed among the top seeds for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification">2018 FIFA World Cup qualification</a> draw. Wales were drawn in Group D with Austria, Serbia, the Republic of Ireland, Moldova and Georgia.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2015, England dropped to tenth in the FIFA rankings, making Wales\xe2\x80\x94in the ninth position\xe2\x80\x94the highest ranked British team for the first time in its history.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In October 2015, Wales attained their highest ever FIFA ranking of eighth. On 10 October 2015, Wales lost 2\xe2\x80\x930 to Bosnia and Herzegovina. However, Wales\' qualification for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">Euro 2016</a> was confirmed after Cyprus defeated Israel that same evening.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Euro_2016">Euro 2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Euro 2016">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wales_Squad_Return,_8th_July_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Wales_Squad_Return%2C_8th_July_2016.jpg/220px-Wales_Squad_Return%2C_8th_July_2016.jpg" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Wales_Squad_Return%2C_8th_July_2016.jpg/330px-Wales_Squad_Return%2C_8th_July_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Wales_Squad_Return%2C_8th_July_2016.jpg/440px-Wales_Squad_Return%2C_8th_July_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="444" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wales_Squad_Return,_8th_July_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Wales team went on an open-top bus tour of Cardiff on their return from Euro 2016.</div></div></div>\n<p>Wales had qualified for Euro 2016 in France, their first European Championship tournament, and were drawn into <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_Group_B" title="UEFA Euro 2016 Group B">Group B</a> with Slovakia, Russia and England. On their Euro debut, on 11 June against Slovakia at the <a href="/wiki/Nouveau_Stade_de_Bordeaux" title="Nouveau Stade de Bordeaux">Nouveau Stade de Bordeaux</a>, Gareth Bale scored direct from a free-kick to give Wales a 1\xe2\x80\x930 lead, and <a href="/wiki/Hal_Robson-Kanu" title="Hal Robson-Kanu">Hal Robson-Kanu</a> scored the winner in a 2\xe2\x80\x931 victory that put them top of the group.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> In their second match, against England in <a href="/wiki/Lens,_Pas-de-Calais" title="Lens, Pas-de-Calais">Lens</a>, Wales led 1\xe2\x80\x930 at half-time through another Bale free-kick, but lost 2\xe2\x80\x931.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Against Russia at the <a href="/wiki/Stadium_Municipal" title="Stadium Municipal">Stadium Municipal</a> in <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>, Aaron Ramsey, <a href="/wiki/Neil_Taylor_(footballer)" title="Neil Taylor (footballer)">Neil Taylor</a> and Bale scored in a 3\xe2\x80\x930 win that made them win the group.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In their round of 16 match at the <a href="/wiki/Parc_des_Princes" title="Parc des Princes">Parc des Princes</a> in Paris, Wales played Northern Ireland and won 1\xe2\x80\x930 after Bale\'s cross was put in as an own goal by <a href="/wiki/Gareth_McAuley" title="Gareth McAuley">Gareth McAuley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In the quarter-final against Belgium, Wales\xe2\x80\x94the last remaining British team\xe2\x80\x94went behind to a long-range effort from <a href="/wiki/Radja_Nainggolan" title="Radja Nainggolan">Radja Nainggolan</a>, but captain Ashley Williams headed an equaliser before Hal Robson-Kanu and <a href="/wiki/Sam_Vokes" title="Sam Vokes">Sam Vokes</a> confirmed a 3\xe2\x80\x931 victory for Wales. This victory advanced Wales to their first major tournament semi-final and also made them the first British nation to advance to the semi-finals of a major tournament since England did so at Euro 1996 as hosts.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first half of the semi-final against <a href="/wiki/Portugal_national_football_team" title="Portugal national football team">Portugal</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a> went goalless, but goals from <a href="/wiki/Cristiano_Ronaldo" title="Cristiano Ronaldo">Cristiano Ronaldo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nani" title="Nani">Nani</a> early in the second half saw Portugal claim a 2\xe2\x80\x930 win.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Wales were welcomed back home on 8 July with an open-top bus parade around Cardiff, starting at <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Castle" title="Cardiff Castle">Cardiff Castle</a> and going past the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a> before finishing at the <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_Stadium" title="Cardiff City Stadium">Cardiff City Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualifiers">2018 FIFA World Cup qualifiers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2018 FIFA World Cup qualifiers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In September 2016, Wales opened their <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification_%E2%80%93_UEFA_Group_D" title="2018 FIFA World Cup qualification \xe2\x80\x93 UEFA Group D">2018 World Cup qualification</a> campaign with a comfortable 4\xe2\x80\x930 home win against Moldova.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> However, they followed this with a run of five consecutive draws away to Austria, at home to Georgia, both home and away against Serbia and away to the Republic of Ireland. That run came to an end with a 1\xe2\x80\x930 home victory over Austria on 2 September 2017, followed by a 2\xe2\x80\x930 away victory against Moldova on 5 September and a 1\xe2\x80\x930 away win over Georgia on 6 October. Wales finished third in their group due to a 1\xe2\x80\x930 loss to the Republic of Ireland on 9 October and failed to qualify for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">final tournament</a> in Russia. Chris Coleman resigned as Wales team manager on 17 November 2017 and was appointed team manager at <a href="/wiki/Sunderland_A.F.C." title="Sunderland A.F.C.">Sunderland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After nearly two months of managerial vacancy, former Wales national player Ryan Giggs was named Wales\' new manager. Giggs, who signed a four-year contract, would be charged with leading Wales\' preparations for the start of the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_UEFA_Nations_League" title="2018\xe2\x80\x9319 UEFA Nations League">2018\xe2\x80\x9319 UEFA Nations League</a> in September 2018 and qualification for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020" title="UEFA Euro 2020">Euro 2020</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium">Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_football_team_home_stadium" title="Wales national football team home stadium">Wales national football team home stadium</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Millennium_Stadium_Cardiff.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Millennium_Stadium_Cardiff.jpg/220px-Millennium_Stadium_Cardiff.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Millennium_Stadium_Cardiff.jpg/330px-Millennium_Stadium_Cardiff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Millennium_Stadium_Cardiff.jpg/440px-Millennium_Stadium_Cardiff.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Millennium_Stadium_Cardiff.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a></div></div></div>\n<p>From 2000\xe2\x80\x932009, Wales played most of their home matches at the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a>, Cardiff. The stadium was built in 1999 on the site of the old <a href="/wiki/National_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="National Stadium">National Stadium</a>, known as <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_Arms_Park" title="Cardiff Arms Park">Cardiff Arms Park</a>, as the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Rugby_Union" title="Welsh Rugby Union">Welsh Rugby Union</a> (WRU) had been chosen to host the <a href="/wiki/1999_Rugby_World_Cup" title="1999 Rugby World Cup">1999 Rugby World Cup</a>. Prior to 1989, Wales played their home games at the grounds of <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swansea_City_A.F.C." title="Swansea City A.F.C.">Swansea City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wrexham_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Wrexham F.C.">Wrexham</a>, but then came to an agreement with the WRU to use Cardiff Arms Park and, subsequently, the Millennium Stadium.\n</p><p>Wales\' first football match at the Millennium Stadium was against Finland on 29 March 2000. The Finns won the match 2\xe2\x80\x931, with <a href="/wiki/Jari_Litmanen" title="Jari Litmanen">Jari Litmanen</a> becoming the first player to score a goal at the stadium. Ryan Giggs scored Wales\' goal in the match, becoming the first Welshman to score at the stadium.\n</p><p>With the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_Stadium" title="Cardiff City Stadium">Cardiff City Stadium</a> in 2009, the FAW chose to stage most home friendlies there, with other friendly matches played at the <a href="/wiki/Liberty_Stadium" title="Liberty Stadium">Liberty Stadium</a> in Swansea and the <a href="/wiki/Racecourse_Ground" title="Racecourse Ground">Racecourse Ground</a> in Wrexham. Qualifying matches continued to be played at the 74,500-capacity Millennium Stadium until the end of 2009, which was typically only around 20\xe2\x80\x9340% full amid poor team results. This led to calls from fans and players for international matches to be held at smaller stadiums. For the Euro 2012 qualifying campaign, the FAW decided Wales would play all of their home matches at either the Cardiff City Stadium or the Liberty Stadium, with the exception of the home tie against England, which was played at the Millennium Stadium. The 2014 World Cup qualifying campaign saw four home matches at the Cardiff City Stadium and one at the Liberty Stadium. Cardiff City Stadium\'s capacity was increased to 33,000 in 2014 and all home matches for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2016 qualifying">Euro 2016 qualifying</a> were scheduled at the stadium and Wales subsequently qualified for the finals tournament in France. All five home qualifiers for the <a href="/wiki/2018_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2018 FIFA World Cup">2018 FIFA World Cup qualification (UEFA)</a> were held at the stadium. Both of the team\'s home <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Nations_League_2018" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Nations League 2018">UEFA Nations League 2018</a> home games are scheduled to take place at the Cardiff City Stadium, together with all home games in the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020_qualifying" title="UEFA Euro 2020 qualifying">Euro 2020 qualifying</a> campaign, however a friendly against Spain will take place at the <a href="/wiki/Principality_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Principality Stadium">Principality Stadium</a> in October 2018 which will be Wales\' first match at the stadium in just over seven-and-a-half years.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Players">Players</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Players">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_squad">Current squad</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Current squad">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following 23 players were called up for the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Nations_League" title="UEFA Nations League">UEFA Nations League</a> match against <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a> on 9 September 2018.\n<br /><i>Caps and goals updated as of 9 September 2018 after the match against <a href="/wiki/Denmark_national_football_team" title="Denmark national football team">Denmark</a>.</i>\n</p>\n<table class="sortable wikitable plainrowheaders" style="font-size:100%; href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Team image">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_coverage">Media coverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Media coverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Live television broadcast rights are held by <a href="/wiki/S4C" title="S4C">S4C</a> (<a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh language</a> commentary) and <a href="/wiki/Sky_Sports" title="Sky Sports">Sky Sports</a> (<a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a> commentary) for qualifiers, and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Sport" title="BBC Sport">BBC Sport</a> for <a href="/wiki/Exhibition_game" title="Exhibition game">friendlies</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colours_and_logo">Colours and logo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wales_national_football_team&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Colours and logo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The primary kit has long been all-red. The crest of the <a href="/wiki/Football_Association_of_Wales" title="Football Association of Wales">Football Association of Wales</a> features a <a href="/wiki/Welsh_Dragon" title="Welsh Dragon">Welsh Dragon</a> on a white shield surrounded by 11 daffodils on a green background, and, since 1951, the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh-language</a> motto <i>Gorau Chwarae Cyd Chwarae</i> ("The best play is team play").<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline"
